           <dt>ba 1</dt>

           <dd>&#x2022; <em>boddhum</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> &amp;c.), to wake, wake up, be awake <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; to recover consciousness (after a swoon) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#K&#x0101;vy&#x00e2;d">K&#x0101;vy&#x00e2;d.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Bha&#x1e6d;&#x1e6d;">Bha&#x1e6d;&#x1e6d;.</a> (aor. Pass. <em>abodhi</em>) </dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; to deem, consider or regard as (with two acc.) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Kath&#x0101;s">Kath&#x0101;s.</a>: Pass. <em>budhyate</em> (aor. <em>abodhi</em>), to be awakened or restored to consciousness </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; See above : Caus. <em>bodh&#x00e1;yati</em>, <em>&#x25cb;te</em> (aor. <em>ab&#x016b;budhat</em> </dd>

           <dt>&#x226b; buddha </dt>
           <dd><em>buddha</em> mfn. awakened, awake <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; expanded, blown <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#S&#x0101;mavBr">S&#x0101;mavBr.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; conscious, intelligent, clever, wise (opp. to <em>m&#x016b;&#x1e0d;ha</em>) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#K&#x0101;v">K&#x0101;v.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; learnt, known, understood <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x0100;past">&#x0100;past.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> ('by', usually instr., but also gen. according to <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#P&#x0101;&#x1e47;">P&#x0101;&#x1e47;.</a> 2-2, 12 ; 3, 67 <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Sch">Sch.</a>) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; m. a wise or learned man, sage <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#W">W.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (with Buddhists) a fully enlightened man who has achieved perfect knowledge of the truth and thereby is liberated from all existence and before his own attainment of Nirv&#x0101;&#x1e47;a reveals the method of obtaining it, (esp.) the principal Buddha of the present age (born at Kapila-vastu about the year 500 B.C. his father, &#x015a;uddhodana, of the &#x015a;&#x0101;kya tribe or family, being the R&#x0101;ja of that district, and his mother, M&#x0101;y&#x0101;-devii, being the daughter of R&#x0101;ja Su-prabuddha <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MWB">MWB.</a> 19 &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; hence he belonged to the Kshatriya caste and his original name &#x015a;&#x0101;kya-muni or &#x015a;&#x0101;kya-si&#x1e43;ha was really his family name, while that of Gautama was taken from the race to which his family belonged </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; for his other names See <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#ib">ib.</a> 23 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; he is said to have died when he was 80 years of age, prob. about 420 B.C. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#ib">ib.</a> 49, n. 1 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; he was preceded by 3 mythical Buddhas of the present Kalpa, or by 24, reckoning previous Kalpa, or according to others by 6 principal Buddhas <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#ib">ib.</a> 136 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; sometimes he is regarded as the 9th incarnation of Vish&#x1e47;u <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Hariv">Hariv.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#K&#x0101;v">K&#x0101;v.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Var">Var.</a> &amp;c.) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; n. knowledge <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#BhP">BhP.</a> (B. <em>buddhi</em>)</dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; Br&#x0101;hmanical explanation, explanations of sacred knowledge or doctrine (esp. for the use of the Br&#x0101;hmans in their sacrifices) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Br">Br.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a portion of the Veda (as distinct from its Mantra and Upanishad portion) and consisting of a class of works called Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;as (they contain rules for the employment of the Mantras or hymns at various sacrifices, with detailed explanations of their origin and meaning and numerous old legends </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; they are said by S&#x0101;ya&#x1e47;a to contain two parts: 1. <em>vidhi</em>, rules or directions for rites </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; 2. <em>artha-v&#x0101;da</em>, explanatory remarks </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; each Veda has its own Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a, that of the <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> is preserved in 2 works, viz. the Aitareya, sometimes called &#x0100;&#x015b;val&#x0101;yana, and the Kaush&#x012b;taki or &#x015a;&#x0101;&#x1e45;kh&#x0101;yana-Br&#x1e6d;Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the white Yajur-veda has the &#x015a;ata-patha-Br&#x1e6d;Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the black Yajur-veda has the Taittir&#x012b;ya-Br&#x1e6d;Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a which differs little from the text of its Sa&#x1e43;hit&#x0101; </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#SV">SV.</a> has 8 Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a, the best known of which are the Prau&#x1e0d;ha or Pa&#x00f1;ca-vi&#x1e43;&#x015b;a and the &#x1e62;a&#x1e0d;vin&#x015b;a </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> has one Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a called Go-patha) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Nir">Nir.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#G&#x1e5b;&#x015a;rS">G&#x1e5b;&#x015a;rS.</a> &amp;c </dd>
